        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2662378496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3050110879617929484">This is my 100th read of 2019 and I’ve now completed my reading challenge 😁<br/><br/>What an amazing book! 4.5 ⭐️<br/><br/><i> "Everytime you take one path, you must live with the memory of the other: of a life left unchosen. Decide as seems best, one course or the other; each way will have its bitter with its sweet." </i><br/><br/>I found this second novel to be just as magical and frightening as book 1. <br/><br/>Vasya has fled the only home she has ever known. After the death of her father and her entire village turning against her. On he</span>
  <span id="freeText3050110879617929484" style="display:none">This is my 100th read of 2019 and I’ve now completed my reading challenge 😁<br /><br />What an amazing book! 4.5 ⭐️<br /><br /><i> "Everytime you take one path, you must live with the memory of the other: of a life left unchosen. Decide as seems best, one course or the other; each way will have its bitter with its sweet." </i><br /><br />I found this second novel to be just as magical and frightening as book 1. <br /><br />Vasya has fled the only home she has ever known. After the death of her father and her entire village turning against her. On her travels she comes across a group of bandits, kidnapping young girls from the surrounding villages. She manages to find one of the camps, rescue the 3 young girls and she rides away she rides into Moscow. The home of the Grand Prince, her monk brother Sasha and her sister Olga. In order to explain how she fought off bandits and rescued the girls, Vasya pretends to be a man. Sasha goes along with it, claiming she is his younger brother.<br /><br />Vasya gains the respect of the Grand Prince, and is invited to stay in Moscow. But her secret cannot stay secret forever, and someone is watching her - someone who knows who she is, and plans to exploit her. <br /><br />Meanwhile, her relationship with the Winter King Morozko, is just as bizarre as ever. I still can't fully get behind it - but that's just me. He keeps an eye on Vasya, and keeps her safe when he can. She still has Solovey, her loyal and powerful horse.<br /><br />But it isn't long until the villain comes to light. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Kasyan, disguised as a noble Lord, but who is actually a deathless sorcerer, kidnaps Vasya's niece Marya. I loved the part where Vasya's grandmother was trapped as a ghost by Kasyan, and Vasya is able to free her and destroy him. He was surviving off of her spirit, which is why he took Marya - hoping to do the same to her.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Vasya must do everything in her power to protect those she loves, with help from the creatures she can see. She is a fantastic protagonist. She will not bow to authority just because she was born a woman, she will be herself whatever the consequences, and I LOVE that.<br /><br />I loved this installment, this series has everything you could need. Sorcery, sword fighting, faith, magical creatures and being true to yourself no matter what.<br /><br />I can't wait to read The Winter of the Witch.<br /><br /><i> "They are all smiles in the court of Sarai -until they set their teeth into your throat and pull." </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3050110879617929484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2124262863" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2124262863" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2124262863?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2124262863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9124119180595208599">Book Two in a Trilogy.....<br/> "The Girl in the Tower", is the sequel to "The Bear and the Nightingale". <br/>which is DAZZLING- GLORIOUS - and SENSATIONAL!!!<br/><br/>Once again, author Katherine Arden has done something really extraordinary-- <br/>she gives us an historical fiction medieval Russian Fairy Tale.....Incredibly creative and breathtaking. <br/>The history itself is educational and fascinating....also barbarous-and complex. It's dangerous times: villages are burning - and people have been killed. <br/><br/>From start to </span>
  <span id="freeText9124119180595208599" style="display:none">Book Two in a Trilogy.....<br /> "The Girl in the Tower", is the sequel to "The Bear and the Nightingale". <br />which is DAZZLING- GLORIOUS - and SENSATIONAL!!!<br /><br />Once again, author Katherine Arden has done something really extraordinary-- <br />she gives us an historical fiction medieval Russian Fairy Tale.....Incredibly creative and breathtaking. <br />The history itself is educational and fascinating....also barbarous-and complex. It's dangerous times: villages are burning - and people have been killed. <br /><br />From start to finish -I was totally melting into this story. Before we enter the wilderness-with Vasilisa Petrovna...(Vasya/Vasilii)....we meet her older sister, Olga Vladimirova -who has two young children and a third one on the way. Olga holds the context of 'the worries' for all her family members -in the way I imagine many first born sisters do. <br />We also meet brother Aleksandr -Sasha... and The Grand Prince of Moscow - Dmitrii- a Priest from Olga's and Vasys's home town of Lesbaya Zemlya. It's at the beginning when we learn from Sasha about the bandits and how strong and organized they seem to be raiding villages. The Priest brings sad news about their father as well. <br /><br />Sasha tries to warn his Royal cousin - Dmitrii...that there must not be a war come spring with the Khan's. It's brutal out there. They need more time to gather more men and he wants Dmitrii to go back with him into the woods. <br /><br />Vasya is already out in those woods - with her Bay Stallion named Solovery. Vasya has a fire for freedom in her belly to explore - to not be confined to marriage or live as a nun in a convent. Taking on the disguise as a boy ( completely sexless)-at times Vasya ---named changed to Vasilii--finds it challenging playing the role of country boy. She knows she shouldn't blush - for example. <br />Vasya is often intrigued by all the new things she sees ( the city was almost too over-stimulating)--yet she is also frightened as can be at times --and COLD. There were times she was shivering convulsively in the night air - with snow falling thicker than ever. <br /><br />I don't want to spoil the story itself --but Vasya with her mare - traveling - and putting herself in dangers way - maturing day by day - and all the supporting characters are absolutely dazzling. There is adventure - suspense - tension - warmth - laughter- and love!!! There was one spot - where I laughed and cried at the 'same' time. My emotions exploded for a few minutes. <br /><br />I'm blessed with the physical books. They are both GORGEOUS!! MANY Thanks to Random House Publishing...... plus, thank you Netgalley! <br /><br />The last person I must say a HUGE THANK YOU TOO is Katherine Arden!!!!<br />The lovely prose had me STOP- RE-READ -and......BASK-with PLEASURE!!! <br /> ......from tinkling of bells, a line of sleighs, lumpish strangers, bristling beards, mittened hands, honeycakes to soothe an irritable Bay Stallion....etc. etc. etc. I was kept in 'aw'!!<br /><br />I can't wait for book Three! -- Sons and Daughters will love these books too!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9124119180595208599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2276015765?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2276015765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2656959172937770318">Vasya is a child no more. <br/><br/>Disguised as a boy, she wanders the forest, set to become a traveler and explore the world she was once kept away from. Unfortunately, the world can be dangerous and the people cruel even to a boy.<br/><br/>If you found The Bear and the Nightingale marvellous, you should have no problem being swept away by this sequel. It contains more action than its predecessor, but it remains a slow-paced character-driven story, fortunately with a lesser focus on religion.<br/><br/>The part where Vasya </span>
  <span id="freeText2656959172937770318" style="display:none">Vasya is a child no more. <br /><br />Disguised as a boy, she wanders the forest, set to become a traveler and explore the world she was once kept away from. Unfortunately, the world can be dangerous and the people cruel even to a boy.<br /><br />If you found The Bear and the Nightingale marvellous, you should have no problem being swept away by this sequel. It contains more action than its predecessor, but it remains a slow-paced character-driven story, fortunately with a lesser focus on religion.<br /><br />The part where Vasya is reacquainted with her older siblings reminded me of the Game of Thrones scene in which Arya sees Sansa after having been separated for so long. Both are happy they are alive and well, but neither of them is able to trust the other completely, so many secrets breathing between them. <br /><br />As always, the story is beautifully-told and the tone serious while still being truthful to the main character’s still young age. I had no clue where the story would be going after reading the first book. I wasn’t sure why these creatures pertaining to the fantasy world were even in it, but now I understand everything better and am all the more eager to read the conclusion because I know the ending will be glorious.<br /><br />But of course, part of me never wants it to end and the other part wishes to become Vasya the Brave! What a memorable heroine. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1925303265" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1925303265" />
    <a title="Diane S ☔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s"><img alt="Diane S ☔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598402138p2/4159922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1925303265?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1925303265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3744272564155182014">4.5 I have never been a fantasy reader, not sure if this is even considered fantasy. I have, however, always enjoyed history and ancient myths. I like to consider these books folklore and legend brought to life, but may be fooling myself. Either way I fell in love with book one, eagerly awaited this book two, fell into both with immense interest and joy.<br/><br/>Medieval Russia, superstitions at the forefront, many believe but few can see these creatures of ancient myth. Those who can risk being labeled </span>
  <span id="freeText3744272564155182014" style="display:none">4.5 I have never been a fantasy reader, not sure if this is even considered fantasy. I have, however, always enjoyed history and ancient myths. I like to consider these books folklore and legend brought to life, but may be fooling myself. Either way I fell in love with book one, eagerly awaited this book two, fell into both with immense interest and joy.<br /><br />Medieval Russia, superstitions at the forefront, many believe but few can see these creatures of ancient myth. Those who can risk being labeled and burned as a witch. Vasya is one, but she is also a young woman who refuses to slot herself into the limited role available to women. Marry young, bear many children or get thyself to the nunnery. I adore this young woman, her fearlessness, how she refuses to settle for less than she thinks she is capable of, and the way she incorporates and uses what she sees. Her magical horse Solovney, who can hear and understand human speech, who protects Vasya,time and time again. The strange background of her own family which comes into play in this outing, when she finds herself in Moscow, disguised as a young boy. The winter king, the man made of ice and snow, death disguised, with his chilling pale blue eyes, who comes to her aid many times. <br /><br />Arden has done such a magnificent job, creating this time period and inserting the reader into the magic that lives all around us if we could only see. There is magic, family, folklore, the arising power of the church, battles, adventure, political uprisings so much. All done cleverly, fitting pieces within pieces to bring color, and personality into this cleverly crafted world. She notes that she has tried to stay true to the history of this period, and this adds an authentic feel to this entertaining story. Such a harsh, bewildering time, so much uncertainty for those in power and those who are not. Now I eagerly await the third in this trilogy, but I already know I will be sad to read the end.<br /><br />ARC from Librarything and edelweiss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3744272564155182014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3298667302" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3298667302" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3298667302?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781473558120" href="/book/show/48983236-the-girl-in-the-tower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=witchy-woman">witchy-woman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=coronavirus-read">coronavirus-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=magic-stuff">magic-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=libby-app">libby-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3298667302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2045413792689602240"><b>Vasya's saga continues.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588435039ra/29398794.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Alright, I was convinced to continue with this series because several friends told me that this book was even better than the 1st book. I wasn't all that sold on the slow pace of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1952187231' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bear and the Nightingale</a> but this one was supposedly where the action happened.<br/>But it didn't. <br/><b>The Girl in the Tower</b> wasn't any better <i>or</i> any worse than its predecessor. It was, for me, exactly the same.<br/>In my opinion, if book 1 didn't rock your socks off then this one won't either.<br/><b>Or maybe it w</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2045413792689602240" style="display:none"><b>Vasya's saga continues.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588435039ra/29398794.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alright, I was convinced to continue with this series because several friends told me that this book was even better than the 1st book. I wasn't all that sold on the slow pace of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1952187231" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bear and the Nightingale</a> but this one was supposedly where the action happened.<br>But it didn't. <br><b>The Girl in the Tower</b> wasn't any better <i>or</i> any worse than its predecessor. It was, for me, exactly the same.<br>In my opinion, if book 1 didn't rock your socks off then this one won't either.<br><b>Or maybe it will?</b> &lt;--<i>I'm only ONE person, what the hell do I know?</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588436672ra/29398919.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Still, there is no getting around the fact that is a very well-written story.<br>Now, the main draw for books like this (to me) is fairytale/folklore stuff. But this one is too rooted in the mundane to get me really excited. Magical snow and wind, understanding horses, or little creatures that live in your oven and protect your house if you feed them bread are all cool, but none of that could really make up for the plodding pace of a story that doesn't really go anywhere super interesting.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588438614ra/29399385.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The gist of the story is that Vasya doesn't want to be hemmed in by the constraints of society because she's a woman. She wants to live her life. Rightly so. But no one else seems to understand why a young woman would want to be anything other than a wife &amp; mother or (better yet) a nun.<br>I thought <b>The Girl in the Tower</b> was excellent at showcasing what it must have been like for any woman who was different in old-timey Russia. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588438614ra/29399386.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There's a budding romance between Vasya and the Frost Demon dude, but it feels kinda weird &amp; boring - not in any way a relationship that I would want to partake in. It's fine for <i>her</i>, I guess, but I certainly didn't catch any feels for him. <br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588439947ra/29399851.gif" width="350" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>There's only one book left and it's not like I hated this one, so I suppose there's no real reason that I shouldn't go ahead and finish the story out.<br>Again, I am <b>NOT</b> saying this is at all an unreadable book, but for readers who are very action-oriented (like me), this one may not seem as enchanting as it might to readers who enjoy dense prose and lush settings.<br><br>Kathleen Gati - Narrator &lt;--she did an excellent job reading this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2045413792689602240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3254661433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_1896139306" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1896139306" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1896139306?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=slavic-motives">slavic-motives</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=i-want-to-marry-him">i-want-to-marry-him</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=3rd-pov">3rd-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=swoon-worthy-hero">swoon-worthy-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=alternative-history">alternative-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=excellent-writing">excellent-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=i-will-go-down-with-this-ship">i-will-go-down-with-this-ship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1896139306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14177255971820864239"><p><b>Every time you take one path, you must live with the memory of the other: of a life left unchosen</b><br/><br/>An adventure Vasya started in book 1 continues in The Girl from the Tower. More action, more folklore, more romance, more political intrigues - book two suppresses its predecessor in every aspect or is it? <br/><br/>One of the most amazing things i loved about the bear and the nightingale - its darkness. Without a doubt the book was a visibly darker interpretation of Russian folklore, which made the story aliv</p></span>
  <span id="freeText14177255971820864239" style="display:none"><p><b>Every time you take one path, you must live with the memory of the other: of a life left unchosen</b><br /><br />An adventure Vasya started in book 1 continues in The Girl from the Tower. More action, more folklore, more romance, more political intrigues - book two suppresses its predecessor in every aspect or is it? <br /><br />One of the most amazing things i loved about the bear and the nightingale - its darkness. Without a doubt the book was a visibly darker interpretation of Russian folklore, which made the story alive with images of night creatures crawling in the cold cold northern winter, growing even more colder, if possible, with every nightmare coming alive in the darkness. The other thing that made the first book memorable for me is the cast of characters. None of them were a hero; they had struggles on their paths and it was clear book 2 would continue with the question: what will become of Vasya, Morozko, Konstantin, Sasha and Olga? I was extremely curious about this question as well.<br /><br />The girl in the tower starts with Vasya on the run from her home where she was considered a witch, thanks to the priest Konstantin's vigilance. She has two choices: either be burnt on pyre as a witch or to be send to live in a convent. Free spirited Vasya, of course. chooses the third option: to run away and ask help from Morozko, the frost demon. But Morozko has his own secrets and Vasya's path will lead her to a different from the initial goal direction. <br /><br />I was highly excited about Vasya going into Moscow. The capital as beautiful as it is dangerous for someone with Vasya's gifts. Everywhere eyes, everywhere plotting and danger behind corners. Even Vasya's siblings Sasha and Olga are not the same people as they were when they left home. And a new mysterious lord Kasyan Lutovich— who seems to be hiding something very important- adds to the pile of intrigues Vasya encounters in the capital. To say that I am satisfied with the direction the plot took in this book? Yes. But was it what I wanted from this book? Not exactly. Let me explain. I thoroughly enjoyed the way Katherine Arden twisted the plot, but I cannot say it was enough to make me surprised or to call political intrigues in this book <i>actual</i> intrigues. Of course, without a doubt, for Vasya it was a new experience as she started as a naive country girl who wanted to see the world, and it's quite understandable that the level of intrigue suits Vasya's perception of the world at the given moment. Alas for me, spoiled with a more prominent subplots and vicious twists in books I am reading, it was not enough to be fully engaged in the mystery Vasya tried to unravel. I already predicted the outcome and knew beforehand every secret that this or that character hid from Vasya. It didn't spoil my enjoyment of the story or characters, but it made it a little bit paler, not so vibrant as it was with the first book. <br /><br />But if the plot failed to surprise me, the characters showed a great deal of potential in this book. Especially Morozko. I already said in my review for book 1 that he is the one character I was intrigued by the most. Well, well, finally we have a glimpse of true frost demon in this book and I loved that he is not so pristine clear and goodie-two-shoes as it might've seemed in book 1. I loved every scene he shared with Vasya in this book and I am looking forward to his role in book 3, which I've heard from the author will be a significant one. <br /><br />As for Vasya herself, I can say the girl is getting older and wiser. In book 1 she was still that naive young child who only was learning her strengths and the world around. In book 2 Vasya shows herself as a very reliable and strong character who learns from her mistakes and opposes those who wish to harm her or people she loves; she turns into a woman: strong and independent *whisper * though I still love that Morozko is always there to save her. Vasya is a female character I can add to my list of favorites. As for the romance, things are getting more clear and steamer, but still I need more development from that side. And judging by the way the book ended, we will have <i>something</i> in book 3 *excited giggle*<br /><br />I don't want to beat around the bush: The bear and the nightingale is fresh and masterly crafted new series that already has a special place in my heart. I recommend it to everyone who wants something new and something magical with a bit of crisp white snow to clear - metaphorically - their minds from everyday problems.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="14177255971820864239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1433075476522759901"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534084017i/26117052.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"Close your eyes," he said into her ear. "Come with me."<br/>She did so, and suddenly she saw what he saw. She was the wind, the clouds gathering in the smoky sky, the thick snow of deep winter. She was nothing. She was everything.</b>
</blockquote><br/>✨ I wish I had thought of a way to create a magical gem in which I'd have kept all the beautiful words because let's face it, my ability to write a review has been seriously fading these past months.<br/><br/>I want to say that <strong><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13922215.Katherine_Arden' rel='nofollow noopener'>Katherine Arden</a>'s writing is so gorgeous and enchant</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText1433075476522759901" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534084017i/26117052.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Close your eyes," he said into her ear. "Come with me."<br>She did so, and suddenly she saw what he saw. She was the wind, the clouds gathering in the smoky sky, the thick snow of deep winter. She was nothing. She was everything.</b>
</blockquote><br>✨ I wish I had thought of a way to create a magical gem in which I'd have kept all the beautiful words because let's face it, my ability to write a review has been seriously fading these past months.<br><br>I want to say that <strong><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13922215.Katherine_Arden" rel="nofollow noopener">Katherine Arden</a>'s writing is so gorgeous and enchanting</strong> that its brilliance inspired me to delve into my forgotten idioms but today, more than ever, my fingers hover above the keyboard and I don't know how to express my love?<br><br>Where are <i>chierti</i> when we need them?<br><br>Oh, well, I'll do my best.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534084017i/26117053.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✨ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34050917-the-girl-in-the-tower" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Tower</a> begins right after the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25489134-the-bear-and-the-nightingale" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bear and the Nightingale</a>, when our beloved Vasya must escape her village, failing which she'd end in a convent, married, or worst if the frightened whispers and the accusations of witchcraft take precedence. She's not about to fulfill the role set out for women in this misogynist society, and would rather explore the world as a boy, thank you very much. But it's without counting on the dangers creeping in, and <strong>soon she finds herself in the midst of Moscow's political and magical intrigues.</strong> <br><br>If you enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25489134-the-bear-and-the-nightingale" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bear and the Nightingale</a>, I can't see why you wouldn't enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34050917-the-girl-in-the-tower" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Tower</a>, given that this sequel keeps everything that made the first book captivating - the <strong>fabulous atmosphere</strong>, the <strong>complex characters</strong>, the <strong>fascinating folklore</strong> - but the stakes are higher and it's just so much more <i>exciting.</i><br><br>I loved everything about it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534084017i/26117054.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✨ If Vasya has a special place in my heart, it's important to note that none of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13922215.Katherine_Arden" rel="nofollow noopener">Katherine Arden</a>'s characters are wasted, or one-dimensional. <strong>All are complex beings caught in a tug of war between opposite forces</strong> and reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34050917-the-girl-in-the-tower" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Tower</a> made the differences with other fantasy works so much more profound because how rare is it, really? <strong>We readers are slowly struck by the realization that <i>there's no such thing as a right choice</i> and actions we support could - and <em>will</em> - have dire consequences.</strong><br><br>And what about the incredible characters' dynamics? The family relationships? It's <em>perfection.</em><br><br>Above everything, I love how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34050917-the-girl-in-the-tower" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Tower</a> <strong>puts great emphasis on the utter brilliance of women, <i>regardless of their choices</i>.</strong> Indeed it would have been so easy to praise Vasya and Vasya only, but that's not what this story is about : with Olga, and others, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13922215.Katherine_Arden" rel="nofollow noopener">Katherine Arden</a> shows other forms of strength, and explores the complex threads of what it means to be a woman in this world, to be <i>brave</i>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b><i>Witch.</i> The word drifted across his mind. <i>We call such women so because we have no other name.</i></b>
</blockquote><br>As for men, <strong>they unsurprisingly don't have a clue what they're doing, but they do it anyway, because #patriarchy.</strong> Yet they're still complex, villains and allies alike, and again, that's what makes it so hard to dismiss them entirely.<br><br>With this in mind, it's no surprise that <b>my favorite male characters are a sassy horse and a frost demon,</b> isn't it? I adore them. I'll protect them at all cost. <b>I am so,so scared.</b><br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534084017i/26117055.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✨ <strong>5 stars, and </strong><strong>I couldn't recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34050917-the-girl-in-the-tower" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl in the Tower</a> enough.</strong> Again, if you liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25489134-the-bear-and-the-nightingale" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bear and the Nightingale</a>, I can't see why you wouldn't fall in love again, and if you haven't read the first book yet? <em>God,</em> what are you waiting for?<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="https://www.Vecteezy.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Art created with the graphics provided by Vecteezy</a><br><br><b>prereview</b> : Why am I not surprised that a fantasy novel that puts great emphasis on the utter brilliance of both women and demons thoroughly won my heart? Also, how come I hate Spring now?</span>
  <a data-text-id="1433075476522759901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2103316589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2103316589" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2103316589?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2103316589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18139226096170689489">We return to the entrancing and magical world of Vasya in medieval Russia. A grief stricken Vasya mourns the loss of Dunya and her father, wanders the icy forests, unable to return to her family home of Lesnaya Zemlya, branded a witch by the locals, threatened with marriage and the convent, choices that are anathema to her. She is naive to the ways of the world, men, political intrigue, ghosts, the fire bird, sorcerers, Moscow and more but she is hungry to see and know more than the small corner</span>
  <span id="freeText18139226096170689489" style="display:none">We return to the entrancing and magical world of Vasya in medieval Russia. A grief stricken Vasya mourns the loss of Dunya and her father, wanders the icy forests, unable to return to her family home of Lesnaya Zemlya, branded a witch by the locals, threatened with marriage and the convent, choices that are anathema to her. She is naive to the ways of the world, men, political intrigue, ghosts, the fire bird, sorcerers, Moscow and more but she is hungry to see and know more than the small corner she has grown up in. She reaches for a new identity and role, despite being exhorted to make other choices by Morozko, the Winter King, the death and frost demon, her monk brother, Sasha, and her sister, Olya, pregnant with her third child. Olya has accepted her fate as a highborn woman, married to an important prince, closeted and restricted, confined to the tower with her two children, Marya and Daniil. The contrast between the two sisters could not be greater, with Vasya caught between two worlds, where she sees what others cannot, her grandmother, Tamara, was the same and another family member is to continue in this tradition. <br /><br />Vasya walks amongst danger, her only recourse for support and help remain the spirits and guardians of the older pagan world, to whom she offers blood tributes, Solovey, her faithful and trusty horse and Morozko. A battle hardened Vasya emerges with a redefined relationship and understanding with the Winter King with the taste of pine on her lips growing ever stronger, in possession of a knife of ice, and her sapphire talisman. Morozko faces the age old quandry, for you cannot love and be immortal. Vasya wants to be a traveller, a feat she can only achieve in disguise as a boy, never a woman. She ventures into villages that are burned down by Tartar bandits and residents murdered, and abducted girls. Vasya joins her cousin, the Grand Prince of Moscow, Sasha and Kasyan Lutovich to find the bandits. An impenetrable shadow hangs over Moscow and the Khans want their contribution, the Grand Prince faces threats, political intrigue, a web of deceit and lies, and where the spirits and guardians hang by a merest of threads. Vasya is surrounded by forces determined on her downfall, both mortal and immortal.<br /><br />This is a much darker tale, remaining faithful to Russian history, whilst drawing on the supernatural magic of its folklore. Arden is a gifted writer, creating a deeply compelling narrative simply drenched in atmosphere that blends the differing threads present in the novel beautifully. She makes the period come alive, the growing influence of Christianity, the strongly entrenched prejudices and attitudes to women, the battles for power and land, and the prominence of the dark fairytales that enchant, like that of the snow child. Vasya is tested to her deepest core, and emerges as woman who knows what she wants and an awareness of the depth of her emotional feelings. She has to negotiate the complexities of sibling relationships and the fantastical world, learning the hard way about the nature of the medieval world she is a part of. All in all, this has turned out to be a worthy sequel to The Bear and the Nightingale, a superlative read that I cannot recommend highly enough. Cannot wait for the final book. Many thanks to Random House Ebury for an ARC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18139226096170689489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1982996212" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1982996212" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475256742p2/41788446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1982996212?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781785031069" href="/book/show/35004343-the-girl-in-the-tower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1982996212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15942506050982047853">I adore the world Katherine Arden has created here. The things I loved, loved, loved about the first part of this series are still all here:<br/><br/>- brilliant characters with believable interactions,<br/>- sibling relationships that are complicated and true,<br/>- an atmosphere so all-encompassing that it makes you forget your own surroundings,<br/>- wonderfully immersive descriptions,<br/>- a surprising and wonderful way to construct sentences that just sound like nobody else (in the best possible way) while still retain</span>
  <span id="freeText15942506050982047853" style="display:none">I adore the world Katherine Arden has created here. The things I loved, loved, loved about the first part of this series are still all here:<br /><br />- brilliant characters with believable interactions,<br />- sibling relationships that are complicated and true,<br />- an atmosphere so all-encompassing that it makes you forget your own surroundings,<br />- wonderfully immersive descriptions,<br />- a surprising and wonderful way to construct sentences that just sound like nobody else (in the best possible way) while still retaining that fairy-talesque rhythm that makes this series so readable,<br />- an understanding of the essence of fairy-tales that shows itself in the brilliant way the familiar tropes are both used and subverted, and<br />- the wonderful setting of Medieval Russia.<br />- And many more things.<br /><br />From the very first chapter I was fully immersed in the story as we follow Vasya fleeing her home town after the events of the last book lest she be burned as a witch. Having only herself and her horse Solovey to rely on, this book has much higher stakes than the first one. Vasya pretends to be a boy and gets not only herself but her older siblings Sasha and Olga caught up in a web of lies.<br /><br />I was not quite as enamored as I was with the first book (although to be fair, that book was one of the best things I have read in years…). Most of that comes down to simple genre preferences. This second book is a lot more fast-paced while the first one created a wonderfully slow narrative with clever twists on familiar fairy tales; this book reads more like a conventional YA-Fantasy (albeit a brilliantly written and very beautiful one). My biggest problem was the “pretending to be someone else”-trope. This is one of my least favourite tropes and stresses me out to no end. The dread this built made this a very different read for me.<br /><br />But beyond this tiny little issue, I was wildly pleased with this book; I adore what Katherine Arden has created here and I find her vision and her voice beyond exciting. I am happy to have been there from the beginning and I cannot imagine not reading each and every single thing she will ever write.<br /><br />First sentence: “A girl rode a bay horse through a forest late at night.”<br /><br />_____<br />I received an arc of this book curtesy of NetGalley and Random House, Ebury Publishing in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15942506050982047853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1983943174" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1983943174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5715645152878358427">!! NOW AVAILABLE !!<br/><br/>Fairy tales were passed from generation to generation through their telling, oral traditions, lessons, cautionary tales. Most fairy tales were born this way, through stories told generation after generation, and then eventually put to print. The original versions of these fairy tales, the ones that we were typically raised on, are not the Disneyfied ones that we think of, cleansed of sex, rape, incest, murder, but still contain a darker side. To balance that darker side, typic</span>
  <span id="freeText5715645152878358427" style="display:none">!! NOW AVAILABLE !!<br /><br />Fairy tales were passed from generation to generation through their telling, oral traditions, lessons, cautionary tales. Most fairy tales were born this way, through stories told generation after generation, and then eventually put to print. The original versions of these fairy tales, the ones that we were typically raised on, are not the Disneyfied ones that we think of, cleansed of sex, rape, incest, murder, but still contain a darker side. To balance that darker side, typically there is the use of enchantment, and often, folkloric characters – fairies, witches, and such, fantasy. <br /><br />As a child, I loved the fairy tales I was read, and then not much later read on my own. A set of 12 books, “My Book House” books, filled with wonderful illustrations from, I believe, the 1920s / 1930s. Darker than the Disney versions, but enticingly lovely in their telling, these wooed me in. <br /><br />So, when I first read Katherine Arden’s “The Bear and the Nightingale,” it was like revisiting those pages, and those feelings. When I heard there was a second one on the horizon, I knew I had to read that one, too, but I was somewhat wary. Could it live up to her first? For me, it did; in some ways, it may have even surpassed it. “The Girl in the Tower” flows more evenly, at least it did for me, and the story has a sense of urgency, while still retaining that aura of otherworldly beauty that drew me in with her first. There are a few new characters, but if you’ve read her first book, you’ll be familiar with most of the cast. If you haven’t read her first, I would recommend you do so before reading this. I think you would appreciate this story more if you read the first in the series prior to reading this. <br /><br />While accusations of witchcraft are still hovering against her in her village of Lesnaya Zemly, in medieval Muscovy, Vasya flees on her trusty steed, Solovey, knowing that he will take her to the places she longs to go, to see the world outside their village. Safely away from the villagers whose wish is to see her be burned as a witch. Vasya leaves with few regrets, she wants to see more than their forest, the church, the bathhouse; she longs to see palaces, cities and the sun on the sea together with Solovey. She wants to see the world and <i>all</i> it has to offer, for she was once shown the world through the eyes of Morozko, the frost-demon; and ever since, she’s known she wants more. Everything she’d been taught about being a woman has chafed at her; she wants more for herself than to marry or to become a nun. <br /><br />Determined, but cautious, she poses as a boy, Vasilii, the masculine form of her name, the feminine formal being Vasalisa, or Vasya, as a nickname. In her journey, she rights some wrongs, attempts to rescue the kidnapped, and through these tasks, her journey brings her into the world of her brother, Sasha, a priest, a monk. Reluctantly, Sasha keeps her secret, no easy task as time goes by and young Vasya begins to mature. Still, she’s proven her worth on the field of battle, and is accepted among the men as Sasha’s young brother. As the court of the Grand Prince shows signs of unrest amidst those determined to take his power, Vasya’s equally determined to prevent that which may prove to be her undoing. <br /><br />Historical facts merged with fictional fragments of fantasy. Fantastical – conceived or appearing as if conceived by an unrestrained imagination. That sums up what Katherine Arden has given us once again; a luminous, fantastical story conceived by her unrestrained imagination. <br /><br /><br /><br />Pub Date: 05 Dec 2017<br />Paperback Available: 28 JUN 2018<br /><br /><br />Many thanks for the ARC provided by Random House</span>
  <a data-text-id="5715645152878358427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1899865156" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1899865156" />
    <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth"><img alt="K. Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606078931p2/17568354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1899865156?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2017</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=imaginative">imaginative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1899865156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10294538659142682666"><b> 4.5 / 5 ~</b><br/><br/>Another brilliant novel by Katherine Arden. After reading three books of hers, I’m beginning to think there’s nothing she can’t write well. <br/><br/>The writing, as expected, was flawless and lyrical. Though, unlike the first novel in the series, this installment moved at a much quicker pace. And although I enjoyed the slow pace of <i>The Bear and the Nightingale</i>, the faster pace in <i>The Girl in the Tower</i> was more fitting since more happened. Or, at least, I felt like more happened. I mean there’s </span>
  <span id="freeText10294538659142682666" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 / 5 ~</b><br /><br />Another brilliant novel by Katherine Arden. After reading three books of hers, I’m beginning to think there’s nothing she can’t write well. <br /><br />The writing, as expected, was flawless and lyrical. Though, unlike the first novel in the series, this installment moved at a much quicker pace. And although I enjoyed the slow pace of <i>The Bear and the Nightingale</i>, the faster pace in <i>The Girl in the Tower</i> was more fitting since more happened. Or, at least, I felt like more happened. I mean there’s traveling to Moscow, more meetings with the Winter King, new characters and storylines, betrayals, magic, deceit, etc. Truthfully, a lot goes on during Vasya’s travels.<br /><br />Unfortunately (but not really), <i>The Girl in the Tower</i> while magical and exciting, didn't hold up to the lyricality and magical feeling I got while reading <i>The Bear and the Nightingale</i>. Both novels are phenomenal, but I felt as though the first book made me <i>feel</i> more; a teenie bit more. Not much. <br /><br />Now, of course, I’m going to continue this lovely series and start book three tomorrow. I must know what’s going to happen to Vasya, Sasha, and Morozko. I’m even curious to see how all the other character storylines are going to end; I can’t wait to see where Arden takes everything. There are so many possibilities!<br /><br />Overall, it’s bittersweet to think this fairytale will end with the next book, and that I won’t be able to read about Vasya and Morozko anymore. It’ll be upsetting for sure — but right now, my mind is just set on starting the next installment and figuring it all out. I need to know.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10294538659142682666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2061050840" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2061050840" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2061050840?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781785031069" href="/book/show/35004343-the-girl-in-the-tower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2061050840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16231523297767117994">I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>Reread Feb 19: still loved it. Magical. Wintery. Goodness. <br/><br/>Well this was truly magical to read. I loved the previous novel in this series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25489134.The_Bear_and_the_Nightingale__Winternight_Trilogy___1_' title='The Bear and the Nightingale (Winternight Trilogy, #1) by Katherine Arden' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bear and the Nightingale</a>, and had high hopes for the follow up. I was not disappointed. Everything I loved from the first novel - the atmospheric setting of medieval Russia, the richness and depth of characters, and a strong background rooted in Russian folklore were developed and expanded up</span>
  <span id="freeText16231523297767117994" style="display:none">I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />Reread Feb 19: still loved it. Magical. Wintery. Goodness. <br /><br />Well this was truly magical to read. I loved the previous novel in this series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25489134.The_Bear_and_the_Nightingale__Winternight_Trilogy___1_" title="The Bear and the Nightingale (Winternight Trilogy, #1) by Katherine Arden" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bear and the Nightingale</a>, and had high hopes for the follow up. I was not disappointed. Everything I loved from the first novel - the atmospheric setting of medieval Russia, the richness and depth of characters, and a strong background rooted in Russian folklore were developed and expanded upon to make one of the best reads of the year.<br /><br />The Girl in the Tower continues to follow Vasya, as she struggles to find herself now she's free from her strict father and the rules she has been made to follow. Above all else she wants freedom. She wants to travel the world with Solovey, her companion horse, and taste the feel of adventure. But the constrictions of her time, and the imminent dangers that face her family in Moscow - particularly her sister Olga and brother Sasha, bring her crashing back to face her responsibilities. The only way to taste the freedom she longs for is to disguise herself as a boy, and join her brother in the hunt for men determined to topple the Grand Prince of Moscow from rule.<br /><br />Mixed in among the politics of a developing nation, we have a story steeped in Russian folklore. The domovoi and creatures of Midnight seen in the previous novel return, and of course we have Morozko - frost demon and Winter king. Slayer of human girl's hearts, and Vasya's lover. Although labeling him this makes it seem everything is black and white, when it's far more complicated than that. Morozko is deeply conflicted in his feelings for Vasya. He is immortal, and should be unable to feel such things as love. Yet he struggles to let her go and lead the life he wants her to live. He's grown attached to things that should be forbidden to him. He's got so much emotional depth as a character, even though his time with Vasya is often so fleeting and void of conversation. Honestly, I think I'm a little bit in love.<br /><br />Vasya has also grown so much as a character since we first saw her in The Bear and the Nightingale, and it's great to see her develop slowly. It's almost as if I've grown up with her, and faced these troubles by her side. She's determined to rule her own life, not needing anyone and anything to do what she wants. Her relationship with her older siblings Olga and Sasha has also developed, now that she's meeting them for the first time as an adult. She's challenging them on an intellectual level, yet she loves them deeply - to the point where she would sacrifice her happiness and freedom to keep them safe. She's not perfect either. She's rash, and bullish - at one point taking someone's choice out of their hands when it is not her decision to make. She's refreshing and wonderful.<br /><br />Father Konstantin also returns - after being banished by Vasya in the previous novel, although he is woefully missing from most of the novel. I enjoy the complexity of his character - his deeply ingrained belief in his faith, yet with a love/hate of Vasya and a yearning to belong.<br /><br />The plot itself to contain all these wonderful characters is great. It's well paced, as we travel with Vasya and Solovey on their journeys around Russia and then onto Moscow with Sasha, and the plot developments largely left me surprised. There's horse races, magic and little girls in danger. Unlike the previous book, I also thought the ending was well defined and didn't end abruptly. I was satisfied (and sad).<br /><br />Honestly, I enjoyed this immeasurably, I can't wait to bring Vasya home one last time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16231523297767117994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2157882460" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2157882460" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28602001-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438967931p2/28602001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2157882460?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/28602001-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35035120-the-girl-in-the-tower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28602001-emma?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2157882460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10827402326597497077">Beautifully realised follow up to the magical <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25489134.The_Bear_and_the_Nightingale__The_Winternight_Trilogy__1_' title='The Bear and the Nightingale (The Winternight Trilogy #1) by Katherine Arden' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bear and the Nightingale</a>, this book builds and expands on both the world and characters we all loved so much in the first instalment.<br/><br/>After a quick flash of Vasya fleeing into the woods after the events at the end of the last book, we are taken into the world of her sister, Olga. If, like me, you worry that the focus has been switched, fear not... we are soon back with our heroine and her faithful horse, Solovey, determined to escape the confines </span>
  <span id="freeText10827402326597497077" style="display:none">Beautifully realised follow up to the magical <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25489134.The_Bear_and_the_Nightingale__The_Winternight_Trilogy__1_" title="The Bear and the Nightingale (The Winternight Trilogy #1) by Katherine Arden" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bear and the Nightingale</a>, this book builds and expands on both the world and characters we all loved so much in the first instalment.<br /><br />After a quick flash of Vasya fleeing into the woods after the events at the end of the last book, we are taken into the world of her sister, Olga. If, like me, you worry that the focus has been switched, fear not... we are soon back with our heroine and her faithful horse, Solovey, determined to escape the confines of her village and accusations of witchcraft. But this is not a girl who is going to accept the traditions and restrictions of Russian society, religion, or her family; she is bold and fearless, she needs to be free and she wants more for herself. And boy do we want more for her, rarely have I cheered on a girl so much. Here we get to see her grow even more into herself, both as a woman and in her special affinity for the <i>domovoi</i>; it would be a remarkable story even without the supernatural. The foundation in both Russian history and folk lore has once again been extensively researched by Arden, illustrated in spectacular detail throughout the book, and infusing the tale with both darkness and enchantment. Yet it is all blended so well together that the reader is drawn into believing Frost demons, spirits, and sorcerers are real. It is unlike anything else out there.<br /><br />The mix of the folk, fantastic, and historical makes this series one of the most appealing and wonderful out there, it's beautiful and fun and worthy of your time. Highly recommended.<br /><br />ARC via Netgalley.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10827402326597497077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z122tvjQzYzoUe5iOVhbNGEpWx3N5mKlEj69mMqUGRAGW6A+xmGnY8nZLFVuuKYoLxfi3UE8ho8ZDGTOeOic7g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LE5HGv+krgE4yUF2y6xxG1y0JPdn2muQpy0i7BEBce5NSFGSwRXE7hlBg0GcTIwHEoqdN+sAj7qsH/u6o330EA==')})
  }

But Vasilisa doesn\'t mind—she spends the winter nights huddled around the embers of a fire with her beloved siblings, listening to her nurse\'s fairy tales. Above all, she loves the chilling story of Frost, the blue-eyed winter demon, who appears in the frigid night to claim unwary souls. Wise Russians fear him, her nurse says, and honor the spirits of house and yard and forest that protect their homes from evil.\n\nAfter Vasilisa\'s mother dies, her father goes to Moscow and brings home a new wife. Fiercely devout, city-bred, Vasilisa\'s new stepmother forbids her family from honoring the household spirits. The family acquiesces, but Vasilisa is frightened, sensing that more hinges upon their rituals than anyone knows.\n\nAnd indeed, crops begin to fail, evil creatures of the forest creep nearer, and misfortune stalks the village. All the while, Vasilisa\'s stepmother grows ever harsher in her determination to groom her rebellious stepdaughter for either marriage or confinement in a convent.\n\nAs danger circles, Vasilisa must defy even the people she loves and call on dangerous gifts she has long concealed—this, in order to protect her family from a threat that seems to have stepped from her nurse\'s most frightening         $('bookCover_25489134').observe('prototip:shown', function () {

          });
